# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

The borrowck rules for proving disjointness are applied from the \"root\" of the\n2: //! borrow forwards, iterating over \"similar\" projections in lockstep until\n3: //! we can prove overlap one way or another. On each step, if we didn't run out of borrow or place, we know that our elements\n7: //! have the same type, and that they only overlap if they are the identical.\n8: //!\n9: //! - `propagate_constraints()` (region_infer/mod.rs:551) - Propagates region constraints through the constraint DAG
- `RegionInferenceContext::solve()` (region_infer/mod.rs:493) - Coordinates the solving pipeline
- `LivenessValues` - Tracks where regions must be live

**4. Two-Phase Borrow Resolution:**
- `TwoPhaseActivation` enum (borrow_set.rs:66) - Tracks borrow activation state
- `insert_as_pending_if_two_phase()` (borrow_set.rs:341) - Defers checking until activation
- `BorrowData` struct (borrow_set.rs:72) - Stores activation location information

The answer file documents the complete MIR analysis chain with file paths, symbols, and a detailed narrative explaining how these components integrate to perform borrow checking on Rust's Mid-level Intermediate Representation.

Associate some local constants with the `'tcx` lifetime\n104: struct TyCtxtConsts<'tcx>(PhantomData<&'tcx ()>);\n105: \n106: impl<'tcx> TyCtxtConsts<'tcx> {\n107:     const DEREF_PROJECTION: &'tcx /// Provider for `query mir_borrowck`. Similar to `typeck`, this must\n115: /// only be called for typeck roots which will then borrowck all\n116: /// nested bodies as well.\n117: fn mir_borrowck(\n118:     tcx: TyCtxt<'_>,\n119:     def: LocalDefId,\n120: ) -> Result<&FxIndexMap<LocalDefId, ty::DefinitionSiteHiddenType<'_>>, ErrorGuaranteed> {\n121:     assert!(!tcx.is_typeck_child(def.to_def_id()));\n122:     let (input_body, _) = tcx.mir_promoted(def);\n123:     debug!(\"run query mir_borrowck: {}\", tcx.def_path_str(def));\n124: \n125:     let input_body: &Body<'_> = &input_body.borrow();\n126:     if let Some(guar) = input_body.tainted_by_errors {\n127:         debug!(\"Skipping borrowck because of tainted body\");\n128:         Err(guar)\n129:     } else if input_body.should_skip() {\n130:         debug!(\"Skipping borrowck because of injected body\");\n131:         let opaque_types = Default::default();\n132:         Ok(tcx.arena.alloc(opaque_types))\n133:     } else {\n134:         let mut root_cx = BorrowCheckRootCtxt::new(tcx, def, None);\n135:         root_cx.do_mir_borrowck();\n136:         root_cx.finalize()\n137:     }\n138: }\n139: \n140: /// Data propagated to the typeck parent by nested items.\n141: /// This should always be empty for the typeck root.\n142: #[derive(Debug)]\n143: struct PropagatedBorrowCheckResults<'tcx> {\n144:     closure_requirements: Option<ClosureRegionRequirements<'tcx>>,\n145:     used_mut_upvars: SmallVec<[FieldIdx; 8]>,\n146: }\n147: \n148: type DeferredClosureRequirements<'tcx> = Vec<(LocalDefId, ty::GenericArgsRef<'tcx>, Locations)>;\n149: \n150: /// After we borrow check a closure, we are left with various\n151: /// requirements that we have inferred between the free regions that\n152: /// appear in the closure's signature or on its field types. These\n153: /// requirements are then verified and proved by the closure's\n154: /// creating function. This struct encodes those requirements.\n155: ///\n156: /// The requirements are listed as being between various `RegionVid`. The 0th\n157: /// region refers to `'static`; subsequent region vids refer to the free\n158: /// regions that appear in the closure (or coroutine's) type, in order of\n159: /// appearance. (This numbering is actually defined by the `UniversalRegions`\n160: /// struct in the NLL region checker. See for example\n161: /// `UniversalRegions::closure_mapping`.) Note the free regions in the\n162: /// closure's signature and captures are erased.\n163: ///\n164: /// Example: If type check produces a closure with the closure args:\n165: ///\n166: /// ```text\n167: /// ClosureArgs = [\n168: ///     'a,                                         // From the parent.\n169: ///     'b,\n170: ///     i8,                                         // the \"closure kind\"\n171: ///     for<'x> fn(&'<erased> &'x u32) -> &'x u32,  // the \"closure signature\"\n172: ///     &'<erased> String,                          // some upvar\n173: /// ]\n174: /// ```\n175: ///\n176: /// We would \"renumber\" each free region to a unique vid, as follows:\n177: ///\n178: /// ```text\n179: /// ClosureArgs = [\n180: ///     '1,                                         // From the parent.\n181: ///     '2,\n182: ///     i8,                                         // the \"closure kind\"\n183: ///     for<'x> fn(&'3 &'x u32) -> &'x u32,         // the \"closure signature\"\n184: ///     &'4 String,                                 // some upvar\n185: /// ]\n186: /// ```\n187: ///\n188: /// Now the code might impose a requirement like `'1: '2`. When an\n189: /// instance of the closure is created, the corresponding free regions\n190: /// can be extracted from its type and constrained to have the given\n191: /// outlives relationship.\n192: #[derive(Clone, Debug)]\n193: pub struct ClosureRegionRequirements<'tcx> {\n194:     /// The number of external regions defined on the closure. In our\n195:     /// example above, it would be 3 -- one for `'static`, then `'1`\n196:     /// and `'2`. This is just used for a sanity check later on, to\n197:     /// make sure that the number of regions we see at the callsite\n198:     /// matches.\n199:     pub num_external_vids: usize,\n200: \n201:     /// Requirements between the various free regions defined in\n202:     /// indices.\n203:     pub outlives_requirements: Vec<ClosureOutlivesRequirement<'tcx>>,\n204: }\n205: \n206: /// Indicates an outlives-constraint between a type or between two\n207: /// free regions declared on the closure.\n208: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]\n209: pub struct ClosureOutlivesRequirement<'tcx> {\n210:     // This region or type ...\n211:     pub subject: ClosureOutlivesSubject<'tcx>,\n212: \n213:     // ... must outlive this one.\n214:     pub outlived_free_region: ty::RegionVid,\n215: \n216:     // If not, report an error here ...\n217:     pub blame_span: Span,\n218: \n219:     // ... due to this reason.\n220:     pub category: ConstraintCategory<'tcx>,\n221: }\n222: \n223: // Make sure this enum doesn't unintentionally grow\n224: #[cfg(target_pointer_width = \"64\")]\n225: rustc_data_structures::static_assert_size!(ConstraintCategory<'_>, 16);\n226: \n227: /// The subject of a `ClosureOutlivesRequirement` -- that is, the thing\n228: /// that must outlive some region.\n229: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]\n230: pub enum ClosureOutlivesSubject<'tcx> {\n231:     /// Subject is a type, typically a type parameter, but could also\n232:     /// be a projection. Indicates a requirement like `T: 'a` being\n233:     /// passed to the caller, where the type here is `T`.\n234:     Ty(ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx>),\n235: \n236:     /// Subject is a free region from the closure. Indicates a requirement\n237:     /// like `'a: 'b` being passed to the caller; the region here is `'a`.\n238:     Region(ty::RegionVid),\n239: }\n240: \n241: /// Represents a `ty::Ty` for use in [`ClosureOutlivesSubject`].\n242: ///\n243: /// This abstraction is necessary because the type may include `ReVar` regions,\n244: /// which is what we use internally within NLL code, and they can't be used in\n245: /// a query response.\n246: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]\n247: pub struct ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx> {\n248:     inner: Ty<'tcx>,\n249: }\n250: // DO NOT implement `TypeVisitable` or `TypeFoldable` traits, because this\n251: // type is not recognized as a binder for late-bound region.\n252: impl<'tcx, I> !TypeVisitable<I> for ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx> {}\n253: impl<'tcx, I> !TypeFoldable<I> for ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx> {}\n254: \n255: impl<'tcx> ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx> {\n256:     /// All regions of `ty` must be of kind `ReVar` and must represent\n257:     /// universal regions *external* to the closure.\n258:     pub fn bind(tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>, ty: Ty<'tcx>) -> Self {\n259:         let inner = fold_regions(tcx, ty, |r, depth| match r.kind() {\n260:             ty::ReVar(vid) => {\n261:                 let br = ty::BoundRegion {\n262:                     var: ty::BoundVar::from_usize(vid.index()),\n263:                     kind: ty::BoundRegionKind::Anon,\n264:                 };\n265:                 ty::Region::new_bound(tcx, depth, br)\n266:             }\n267:             _ => bug!(\"unexpected region in ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy: {r:?}\"),\n268:         });\n269: \n270:         Self { inner }\n271:     }\n272: \n273:     pub fn instantiate(\n274:         self,\n275:         tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n276:         mut map: impl FnMut(ty::RegionVid) -> ty::Region<'tcx>,\n277:     ) -> Ty<'tcx> {\n278:         fold_regions(tcx, self.inner, |r, depth| match r.kind() {\n279:             ty::ReBound(ty::BoundVarIndexKind::Bound(debruijn), br) => {\n280:                 debug_assert_eq!(debruijn, depth);\n281:                 map(ty::RegionVid::from_usize(br.var.index()))\n282:             }\n283:             _ => bug!(\"unexpected region {r:?}\"),\n284:         })\n285:     }\n286: }\n287: \n288: struct CollectRegionConstraintsResult<'tcx> {\n289:     infcx: .map(|(borrows, uninits, ever_inits)| BorrowckDomain { borrows, uninits, ever_inits })\n633:             .collect();\n634: \n635:     Results { analysis, entry_states }\n636: }\n637: \n638: pub(crate) Debug)]\n1041: enum ArtificialField {\n1042:     ArrayLength,\n1043:     FakeBorrow,\n1044: }\n1045: \n1046: #[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Debug)]\n1047: enum AccessDepth {\n1048:     /// From the RFC: \"A *shallow* access means that the immediate\n1049:     /// fields reached at P are accessed, but references or pointers\n1050:     /// found within are not dereferenced. Right now, the only access\n1051:     /// that is shallow is an assignment like `x = ...;`, which would\n1052:     /// be a *shallow write* of `x`.\"\n1053:     Shallow(Option<ArtificialField>),\n1054: \n1055:     /// From the RFC: \"A *deep* access means that all data reachable\n1056:     /// through the given place may be invalidated or accesses by\n1057:     /// this action.\"\n1058:     Deep,\n1059: \n1060:     /// Access is Deep only when there is a Drop implementation that\n1061:     /// can reach the data behind the reference.\n1062:     Drop,\n1063: }\n1064: \n1065: /// Kind of access to a value: read or write\n1066: /// (For informational purposes only)\n1067: #[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Debug)]\n1068: enum ReadOrWrite {\n1069:     /// From the RFC: \"A *read* means that the existing data may be\n1070:     /// read, but will not be changed.\"\n1071:     Read(ReadKind),\n1072: \n1073:     /// From the RFC: \"A *write* means that the data may be mutated to\n1074:     /// new values or otherwise invalidated (for example, it could be\n1075:     /// de-initialized, as in a move operation).\n1076:     Write(WriteKind),\n1077: \n1078:     /// For two-phase borrows, we distinguish a reservation (which is treated\n1079:     /// like a Read) from an activation (which is treated like a write), and\n1080:     /// each of those is furthermore distinguished from Reads/Writes above.\n1081:     Reservation(WriteKind),\n1082:     Activation(WriteKind, BorrowIndex),\n1083: }\n1084: \n1085: /// Kind of read access to a value\n1086: /// (For informational purposes only)\n1087: #[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Debug)]\n1088: enum ReadKind {\n1089:     Borrow(BorrowKind),\n1090: StorageDeadOrDrop,\n1098:     Replace,\n1099:     MutableBorrow(BorrowKind),\n1100:     Mutate,\n1101:     Move,\n1102: }\n1103: \n1104: /// When checking permissions for a place access, this flag is             // closure from a shared reference.\n1661:                         //\n1662:                         // As such we have to search for the local that this\n1663:                         //         (Deep, Read(ReadKind::Copy)),\n1720:                     LocalMutationIsAllowed::No,\n1721:                     state,\n1722:                 );\n1723: \n1724:                 // Finally, Operand::Constant(_) => {}\n1754:         }\n1755:     }\n1756: \n1757:     /// Checks whether a borrow of this place is invalidated when the function\n1758:     /// exits\n1759:     #[instrument(level = \"debug\", skip(self))]\n1760:     fn check_for_invalidation_at_exit(\n1761:         &mut self,\n1762:         location: Location,\n1763:         borrow: &BorrowData<'tcx>,\n1764:         span: Span,\n1765:     ) {\n1766:         let place = borrow.borrowed_place;\n1767:         let mut root_place = PlaceRef { local: place.local, projection: &[] };\n1768: \n1769:         // location,\n1801:                 borrow,\n1802:                 (place, span),\n1803:                 None,\n1804:             )\n1805:         }\n1806:     }\n1807: \n1808:     /// Reports an error fn check_if_full_path_is_moved(\n1982:         &mut self,\n1983:         location: Location,\n1984:         desired_action: InitializationRequiringAction,\n1985:         place_span: (PlaceRef<'tcx>, Span),\n1986:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n1987:     ) {\n1988:         let maybe_uninits = &state.uninits;\n1989: \n1990:         // Bad scenarios:\n1991:         //\n1992:         // 1. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a.b.c`\n1993:         // 2. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a.b.c.d` (without first reinitializing `a.b.c.d`)\n1994:         // 3. Uninitialized `(a.b.c: &_)`, use of `*a.b.c`; note that with\n1995:         //    partial initialization support, one might have `a.x`\n1996:         //    initialized but not `a.b`.\n1997:         //\n1998:         // OK scenarios:\n1999:         //\n2000:         // 4. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a.b.d`\n2001:         // 5. Uninitialized `a.x`, initialized `a.b`, use of `a.b`\n2002:         // 6. Copied `(a.b: &_)`, use of `*(a.b).c`; note that `a.b`\n2003:         //    must have been initialized for the use to be sound.\n2004:         // 7. Move of `a.b.c` then reinit of `a.b.c.d`, use of `a.b.c.d`\n2005: \n2006:         // The dataflow tracks shallow prefixes distinctly (that is,\n2007:         // field-accesses on P distinctly from P itself), in order to\n2008:         // track substructure initialization separately from the whole\n2009:         // structure.\n2010:         //\n2011:         // E.g., when looking at (*a.b.c).d, if the closest prefix for\n2012:         // which we have a MovePath is `a.b`, then that means that the\n2013:         // initialization state of `a.b` is all we need to inspect to\n2014:         // know if `a.b.c` is valid (and from that we infer that the\n2015:         // dereference and `.d` access is also valid, since we assume\n2016:         // `a.b.c` is assigned a reference to an initialized and\n2017:         // well-formed record structure.)\n2018: \n2019:         // Therefore, if we seek out the *closest* prefix for which we\n2020:         // have a MovePath, that should capture the initialization\n2021:         // state for the place scenario.\n2022:         //\n2023:         // This code covers scenarios 1, 2, and 3.\n2024: \n2025:         debug!(\"check_if_full_path_is_moved place: {:?}\", place_span.0);\n2026:         let (prefix, mpi) = self.move_path_closest_to(place_span.0);\n2027:         if maybe_uninits.contains(mpi) {\n2028:             self.report_use_of_moved_or_uninitialized(\n2029:                 location,\n2030:                 desired_action,\n2031:                 (prefix, place_span.0, place_span.1),\n2032:                 mpi,\n2033:             );\n2034:         } // Only query longest prefix with a MovePath, not further\n2035:         // ancestors; dataflow recurs on children when parents\n2036:         // move (to support partial (re)inits).\n2037:         //\n2038:         // (I.e., querying parents breaks scenario 7; but may want\n2039:         // to do such a query based on partial-init feature-gate.)\n2040:     }\n2041: \n2042:     /// Subslices correspond to multiple move paths, so we iterate through the\n2043:     /// elements of the base array. For each element we check\n2044:     ///\n2045:     /// * Does this element overlap with our slice.\n2046:     /// * Is any part of it uninitialized.\n2047:     fn check_if_subslice_element_is_moved(\n2048:         &mut self,\n2049:         location: Location,\n2050:         desired_action: InitializationRequiringAction,\n2051:         place_span: (PlaceRef<'tcx>, Span),\n2052:         maybe_uninits: &MixedBitSet<MovePathIndex>,\n2053:         from: u64,\n2054:         to: u64,\n2055:     ) {\n2056:         if let Some(mpi) = self.move_path_for_place(place_span.0) {\n2057:             let move_paths = &self.move_data.move_paths;\n2058: \n2059:             let root_path = &move_paths[mpi];\n2060:             for (child_mpi, child_move_path) in root_path.children(move_paths) {\n2061:                 let last_proj = child_move_path.place.projection.last().unwrap();\n2062:                 if let ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { offset, from_end, .. } = last_proj {\n2063:                     debug_assert!(!from_end, \"Array constant indexing shouldn't be `from_end`.\");\n2064: \n2065:                     if (from..to).contains(offset) {\n2066:                         let uninit_child =\n2067:                             self.move_data.find_in_move_path_or_its_descendants(child_mpi, |mpi| {\n2068:                                 maybe_uninits.contains(mpi)\n2069:                             });\n2070: \n2071:                         if let Some(uninit_child) = uninit_child {\n2072:                             self.report_use_of_moved_or_uninitialized(\n2073:                                 location,\n2074:                                 desired_action,\n2075:                                 (place_span.0, place_span.0, place_span.1),\n2076:                                 uninit_child,\n2077:                             );\n2078:                             return; // don't bother finding other problems.\n2079:                         }\n2080:                     }\n2081:                 }\n2082:             }\n2083:         }\n2084:     }\n2085: \n2086:     fn check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved(\n2087:         &mut self,\n2088:         location: Location,\n2089:         desired_action: InitializationRequiringAction,\n2090:         place_span: (PlaceRef<'tcx>, Span),\n2091:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n2092:     ) {\n2093:         let maybe_uninits = &state.uninits;\n2094: \n2095:         // Bad scenarios:\n2096:         //\n2097:         // 1. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a` or `a.b`\n2098:         //    partial initialization support, one might have `a.x`\n2099:         //    initialized but not `a.b`.\n2100:         // 2. All bad scenarios from `check_if_full_path_is_moved`\n2101:         //\n2102:         // OK scenarios:\n2103:         //\n2104:         // 3. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a.b.d`\n2105:         // 4. Uninitialized `a.x`, initialized `a.b`, use of `a.b`\n2106:         // 5. Copied `(a.b: &_)`, use of `*(a.b).c`; note that `a.b`\n2107:         //    must have been initialized for the use to be sound.\n2108:         // 6. This is scenario 3 above.\n2131:         //\n2132:         // (Distinct from handling of scenarios 1+2+4 above because\n2133:         // `place` does not interfere with suffixes of its prefixes,\n2134:         // e.g., `a.b.c` does not interfere with `a.b.d`)\n2135:         //\n2136:         // This code covers scenario 1.\n2137: \n2138:         debug!(\"check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved place: {:?}\", place_span.0);\n2139:         if let Some(mpi) = self.move_path_for_place(place_span.0) {\n2140:             let uninit_mpi = self\n2141:                 .move_data\n2142:                 .find_in_move_path_or_its_descendants(mpi, |mpi| maybe_uninits.contains(mpi));\n2143: \n2144:             if let Some(uninit_mpi) = uninit_mpi {\n2145:                 self.report_use_of_moved_or_uninitialized(\n2146:                     location,\n2147:                     desired_action,\n2148:                     (place_span.0, place_span.0, place_span.1),\n2149:                     uninit_mpi,\n2150:                 );\n2151:                 return; // don't bother finding other problems.\n2152:             }\n2153:         }\n2154:     }\n2155: \n2156:     /// Currently MoveData does not store entries for all places in\n2157:     /// the input MIR. For example it will currently filter out\n2158:     /// places that are Copy; thus we do not track places of shared\n2159:     /// reference type. This routine will walk up a place along its\n2160:     /// prefixes, searching for a foundational place that *is*\n2161:     /// tracked in the MoveData.\n2162:     ///\n2163:     /// An Err result includes a tag indicated why the search failed.\n2164:     /// Currently this can only occur if the place is built off of a\n2165:     /// static variable, as we do not track those in the MoveData.\n2166:     fn move_path_closest_to(&mut self, place: PlaceRef<'tcx>) -> (PlaceRef<'tcx>, MovePathIndex) {\n2167:         match self.move_data.rev_lookup.find(place) {\n2168:             LookupResult::Parent(Some(mpi)) | LookupResult::Exact(mpi) => {\n2169:                 (self.move_data.move_paths[mpi].place.as_ref(), mpi)\n2170:             }\n2171:             LookupResult::Parent(None) => panic!(\"should have move path for every Local\"),\n2172:         }\n2173:     }\n2174: \n2175:     fn move_path_for_place(&mut self, place: PlaceRef<'tcx>) -> Option<MovePathIndex> {\n2176:         // If returns None, then there is no move path corresponding\n2177:         // to a direct owner of `place` (which means there is nothing\n2178:         // that borrowck tracks for its analysis).\n2179: \n2180:         match self.move_data.rev_lookup.find(place) {\n2181:             LookupResult::Parent(_) => None,\n2182:             LookupResult::Exact(mpi) => Some(mpi),\n2183:         }\n2184:     }\n2185: \n2186:     fn check_if_assigned_path_is_moved(\n2187:         &mut self,\n2188:         location: Location,\n2189:         (place, span): (Place<'tcx>, Span),\n2190:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n2191:     ) {\n2192:         debug!(\"check_if_assigned_path_is_moved place: {:?}\", place);\n2193: \n2194:         // None case => assigning to `x` does not require `x` be initialized.\n2195:         for (place_base, elem) in place.iter_projections().rev() {\n2196:             match elem {\n2197:                 ProjectionElem::Index(_/*operand*/) |\n2198:                 ProjectionElem::OpaqueCast(_) |\n2199:                 ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { .. } |\n2200:                 // assigning to P[i] requires P to be valid.\n2201:                 ProjectionElem::Downcast(_/*adt_def*/, _/*variant_idx*/) =>\n2202:                 // assigning to (P->variant) is okay if assigning to `P` is okay\n2203:                 //\n2204:                 // FIXME: is this true even if P is an adt with a dtor?\n2205:                 { }\n2206: \n2207:                 ProjectionElem::UnwrapUnsafeBinder(_) => {\n2208:                     check_parent_of_field(self, location, place_base, span, state);\n2209:                 }\n2210: \n2211:                 // assigning to (*P) requires P to be initialized\n2212:                 ProjectionElem::Deref => {\n2213:                     self.check_if_full_path_is_moved(\n2214:                         location, InitializationRequiringAction::Use,\n2215:                         (place_base, span), state);\n2216:                     // (base initialized; no need to\n2217:                     // recur further)\n2218:                     break;\n2219:                 }\n2220: \n2221:                 ProjectionElem::Subslice { .. } => {\n2222:                     panic!(\"we don't allow assignments to subslices, location: {location:?}\");\n2223:                 }\n2224: \n2225:                 ProjectionElem::Field(..) => {\n2226:                     // if type of `P` has a dtor, then\n2227:                     // assigning to `P.f` requires `P` itself\n2228:                     // be already initialized\n2229:                     let tcx = self.infcx.tcx;\n2230:                     let    self.check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved(\n2234:                                 location, InitializationRequiringAction::Assignment,\n2235:                                 (place_base, span), state);\n2236: \n2237:                             // (base initialized; no need to\n2238:                             // recur further)\n2239:                             break;\n2240:                         }\n2241: \n2242:                         // Once `let s; s.x = V; read(s.x);`,\n2243:                         // is allowed, remove this match arm.\n2244:                         ty::Adt(..) | ty::Tuple(..) => {\n2245:                             check_parent_of_field(self, location, place_base, span, state);\n2246:                         }\n2247: \n2248:                         _ => {}\n2249:                     }\n2250:                 }\n2251:             }\n2252:         }\n2253: \n2254:         fn check_parent_of_field<'a, 'tcx>(\n2255:             this: &mut MirBorrowckCtxt<'a, '_, 'tcx>,\n2256:             location: Location,\n2257:             base: PlaceRef<'tcx>,\n2258:             span: Span,\n2259:             state: &BorrowckDomain,\n2260:         ) {\n2261:             // rust-lang/rust#21232: Until Rust allows reads from the\n2262:             // initialized parts of partially initialized structs, we\n2263:             // will, starting with   "content": "{\"content\":\"1: //! The borrowck rules for proving disjointness are applied from the \\\"root\\\" of the\\n2: //! borrow forwards, iterating over \\\"similar\\\" projections in lockstep until\\n3: //! we can prove overlap one way or another. Essentially, we treat `Overlap` as\\n4: //! a monoid and report a conflict if the product ends up not being `Disjoint`.\\n5: //!\\n6: //! On each step, if we didn't run out of borrow or place, we know that our elements\\n7: //! have the same type, and that they only overlap if they are the identical.\\n8: //!\\n9: //! For example, if we are comparing these:\\n10: //! ```text\\n11: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\\n12: //! ACCESS:  (*x1[i].y).w.b\\n13: //! ```\\n14: //!\\n15: //! Then our steps are:\\n16: //! ```text\\n17: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\\n18: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\\n19: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n20: //!      *x1[2].y    |  *x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n21: //!     (*x1[2].y).z | (*x1[i].y).w  -- we are disjoint and don't need to check more!\\n22: //! ```\\n23: //!\\n24: //! Because `zip` does potentially bad things to the iterator inside, this loop\\n25: //! also handles the case where the access might be a *prefix* of the borrow, e.g.\\n26: //!\\n27: //! ```text\\n28: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\\n29: //! ACCESS:  x1[i].y\\n30: //! ```\\n31: //!\\n32: //! Then our steps are:\\n33: //! ```text\\n34: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\\n35: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\\n36: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n37: //! ```\\n38: //!\\n39: //! -- here we run out of access - the borrow can access a part of it. If this\\n40: //! is a full deep access, then we *know* the borrow conflicts with it. However,\\n41: //! if the access is shallow, then we can proceed:\\n42: //!\\n43: //! ```text\\n44: //!       x1[2].y    | (*x1[i].y)    -- a deref! the access can't get past this, so we\\n45: //!                                     are disjoint\\n46: //! ```\\n47: //!\\n48: //! Our invariant is, that at each step of the iteration:\\n49: //!  - If we didn't run out of access to match, our borrow and access are comparable\\n50: //!    and either equal or disjoint.\\n51: //!  - If we did run out of access, the borrow can access a part of it.\\n52: \\n53: use std::cmp::max;\\n54: use std::iter;\\n55: \\n56: use rustc_hir as hir;\\n57: use rustc_middle::bug;\\n58: use rustc_middle::mir::{\\n59:     Body, BorrowKind, FakeBorrowKind, MutBorrowKind, Place, PlaceElem, PlaceRef, ProjectionElem,\\n60: };\\n61: use rustc_middle::ty::{self, TyCtxt};\\n62: use tracing::{debug, instrument};\\n63: \\n64: use crate::{AccessDepth, ArtificialField, Deep, Overlap, Shallow};\\n65: \\n66: /// When checking if a place conflicts with another place, this enum is used to influence decisions\\n67: /// where a place might be equal or disjoint with another place, such as if `a[i] == a[j]`.\\n68: /// `PlaceConflictBias::Overlap` would bias toward assuming that `i` might equal `j` and that these\\n69: /// places overlap. `PlaceConflictBias::NoOverlap` assumes that for the purposes of the predicate\\n70: /// being run in the calling context, the conservative choice is to assume the compared indices\\n71: /// are disjoint (and therefore, do not overlap).\\n72: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug, Eq, PartialEq)]\\n73: pub enum PlaceConflictBias {\\n74:     Overlap,\\n75:     NoOverlap,\\n76: }\\n77: \\n78: /// Helper function for checking if places conflict with a mutable borrow and deep access depth.\\n79: /// This is used to check for places conflicting outside of the borrow checking code (such as in\\n80: /// dataflow).\\n81: pub fn places_conflict<'tcx>(\\n82:     tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\\n83:     body: &Body<'tcx>,\\n84:     borrow_place: Place<'tcx>,\\n85:     access_place: Place<'tcx>,\\n86:     bias: PlaceConflictBias,\\n87: ) -> bool {\\n88:     borrow_conflicts_with_place(\\n89:         tcx,\\n90:         body,\\n91:         borrow_place,\\n92:         BorrowKind::Mut { kind: MutBorrowKind::TwoPhaseBorrow },\\n93:         access_place.as_ref(),\\n94:         AccessDepth::Deep,\\n95:         bias,\\n96:     )\\n97: }\\n98: \\n99: /// Checks whether the `borrow_place` conflicts with the `access_place` given a borrow kind and\\n100: /// access depth. The `bias` parameter is used to determine how the unknowable (comparing runtime\\n101: /// array indices, for example) should be interpreted - this depends on what the caller wants in\\n102: /// order to make the conservative choice and preserve soundness.\\n103: #[inline]\\n104: pub(super) fn borrow_conflicts_with_place<'tcx>(\\n105:     tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\\n106:     body: &Body<'tcx>,\\n107:     borrow_place: Place<'tcx>,\\n108:     borrow_kind: BorrowKind,\\n109:     access_place: PlaceRef<'tcx>,\\n110:     access: AccessDepth,\\n111:     bias: PlaceConflictBias,\\n112: ) -> bool {\\n113:     let borrow_local = borrow_place.local;\\n114:     let access_local = access_place.local;\\n115: \\n116:     if borrow_local != access_local {\\n117:         // We have proven the borrow disjoint - further projections will remain disjoint.\\n118:         return false;\\n119:     }\\n120: \\n121:     // This Local/Local case is handled by the more general code below, but\\n122:     // it's so common that it's a speed win to check for it first.\\n123:     if borrow_place.projection.is_empty() && access_place.projection.is_empty() {\\n124:         return true;\\n125:     }\\n126: \\n127:     place_components_conflict(tcx, body, borrow_place, borrow_kind, access_place, access, bias)\\n128: }\\n129: \\n130: #[instrument(level = \\\"debug\\\", skip(tcx, body))]\\n131: fn place_components_conflict<'tcx>(\\n132:     tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\\n133:     body: &Body<'tcx>,\\n134:     borrow_place: Place<'tcx>,\\n135:     borrow_kind: BorrowKind,\\n136:     access_place: PlaceRef<'tcx>,\\n137:     access: AccessDepth,\\n138:     bias: PlaceConflictBias,\\n139: ) -> bool {\\n140:     let borrow_local = borrow_place.local;\\n141:     let access_local = access_place.local;\\n142:     // borrow_conflicts_with_place should have checked that.\\n143:     assert_eq!(borrow_local, access_local);\\n144: \\n145:     // loop invariant: borrow_c is always either equal to access_c or disjoint from it.\\n146:     for ((borrow_place, borrow_c), &access_c) in\\n147:         iter::zip(borrow_place.iter_projections(), access_place.projection)\\n148:     {\\n149:         debug!(?borrow_c, ?access_c);\\n150: \\n151:         // Borrow and access path both have more components.\\n152:         //\\n153:         // Examples:\\n154:         //\\n155:         // - borrow of `a.(...)`, access to `a.(...)`\\n156:         // - borrow of `a.(...)`, access to `b.(...)`\\n157:         //\\n158:         // Here we only see the components we have checked so\\n159:         // far (in our examples, just the first component). We\\n160:         // check whether the components being borrowed vs\\n161:         // accessed are disjoint (as in the second example,\\n162:         // but not the first).\\n163:         match place_projection_conflict(tcx, body, borrow_place, borrow_c, access_c, bias) {\\n164:             Overlap::Arbitrary => {\\n165:                 // We have encountered different fields of potentially\\n166:                 // the same union - the borrow now partially overlaps.\\n167:                 //\\n168:                 // There is no *easy* way of comparing the fields\\n169:                 // further on, because they might have different types\\n170:                 // (e.g., borrows of `u.a.0` and `u.b.y` where `.0` and\\n171:                 // `.y` come from different structs).\\n172:                 //\\n173:                 // We could try to do some things here - e.g., count\\n174:                 // dereferences - but that's probably not a good\\n175:                 // idea, at least for now, so just give up and\\n176:                 // report a conflict. This is unsafe code anyway so\\n177:                 // the user could always use raw pointers.\\n178:                 debug!(\\\"arbitrary -> conflict\\\");\\n179:                 return true;\\n180:             }\\n181:             Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint => {\\n182:                 // This is the recursive case - proceed to the next element.\\n183:             }\\n184:             Overlap::Disjoint => {\\n185:                 // We have proven the borrow disjoint - further\\n186:                 // projections will remain disjoint.\\n187:                 debug!(\\\"disjoint\\\");\\n188:                 return false;\\n189:             }\\n190:         }\\n191:     }\\n192: \\n193:     if borrow_place.projection.len() > access_place.projection.len() {\\n194:         for (base, elem) in borrow_place.iter_projections().skip(access_place.projection.len()) {\\n195:             // Borrow path is longer than the access path. Examples:\\n196:             //\\n197:             // - borrow of `a.b.c`, access to `a.b`\\n198:             //\\n199:             // Here, we know that the borrow can access a part of\\n200:             // our place. This is a conflict if that is a part our\\n201:             // access cares about.\\n202: \\n203:             let base_ty = base.ty(body, tcx).ty;\\n204: \\n205:             match (elem, base_ty.kind(), access) {\\n206:                 (_, _, Shallow(Some(ArtificialField::ArrayLength)))\\n207:                 | (_, _, Shallow(Some(ArtificialField::FakeBorrow))) => {\\n208:                     // The array length is like additional fields on the\\n209:                     // type; it does not overlap any existing data there.\\n210:                     // Furthermore, if cannot actually be a prefix of any\\n211:                     // borrowed place (at least in MIR as it is currently.)\\n212:                     //\\n213:                     // e.g., a (mutable) borrow of `a[5]` while we read the\\n214:                     // array length of `a`.\\n215:                     debug!(\\\"borrow_conflicts_with_place: implicit field\\\");\\n216:                     return false;\\n217:                 }\\n218: \\n219:                 (ProjectionElem::Deref, _, Shallow(None)) => {\\n220:                     // e.g., a borrow of `*x.y` while we shallowly access `x.y` or some\\n221:                     // prefix thereof - the shallow access can't touch anything behind\\n222:                     // the pointer.\\n223:                     debug!(\\\"borrow_conflicts_with_place: shallow access behind ptr\\\");\\n224:                     return false;\\n225:                 }\\n226:                 (ProjectionElem::Deref, ty::Ref(_, _, hir::Mutability::Not), _) => {\\n227:                     // Shouldn't be tracked\\n228:                     bug!(\\\"Tracking borrow behind shared reference.\\\");\\n229:                 }\\n230:                 (ProjectionElem::Deref, ty::Ref(_, _, hir::Mutability::Mut), AccessDepth::Drop) => {\\n231:                     // Values behind a mutable reference are not access either by dropping a\\n232:                     // value, or by StorageDead\\n233:                     debug!(\\\"borrow_conflicts_with_place: drop access behind ptr\\\");\\n234:                     return false;\\n235:                 }\\n236: \\n237:                 (ProjectionElem::Field { .. }, ty::Adt(def, _), AccessDepth::Drop) => {\\n238:                     // Drop can read/write arbitrary projections, so places\\n239:                     // conflict regardless of further projections.\\n240:                     if def.has_dtor(tcx) {\\n241:                         return true;\\n242:                     }\\n243:                 }\\n244: \\n245:                 (ProjectionElem::Deref, _, Deep)\\n246:                 | (ProjectionElem::Deref, _, AccessDepth::Drop)\\n247:                 | (ProjectionElem::Field { .. }, _, _)\\n248:                 | (ProjectionElem::Index { .. }, _, _)\\n249:                 | (ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { .. }, _, _)\\n250:                 | (ProjectionElem::Subslice { .. }, _, _)\\n251:                 | (ProjectionElem::OpaqueCast { .. }, _, _)\\n252:                 | (ProjectionElem::Downcast { .. }, _, _)\\n253:                 | (ProjectionElem::UnwrapUnsafeBinder(_), _, _) => {\\n254:                     // Recursive case. This can still be disjoint on a\\n255:                     // further iteration if this a shallow access and\\n256:                     // there's a deref later on, e.g., a borrow\\n257:                     // of `*x.y` while accessing `x`.\\n258:                 }\\n259:             }\\n260:         }\\n261:     }\\n262: \\n263:     // Borrow path ran out but access path may not\\n264:     // have. Examples:\\n265:     //\\n266:     // - borrow of `a.b`, access to `a.b.c`\\n267:     // - borrow of `a.b`, access to `a.b`\\n268:     //\\n269:     // In the first example, where we didn't run out of\\n270:     // access, the borrow can access all of our place, so we\\n271:     // have a conflict.\\n272:     //\\n273:     // If the second example, where we did, then we still know\\n274:     // that the borrow can access a *part* of our place that\\n275:     // our access cares about, so we still have a conflict.\\n276:     if borrow_kind == BorrowKind::Fake(FakeBorrowKind::Shallow)\\n277:         && borrow_place.projection.len() < access_place.projection.len()\\n278:     {\\n279:         debug!(\\\"borrow_conflicts_with_place: shallow borrow\\\");\\n280:         false\\n281:     } else {\\n282:         debug!(\\\"borrow_conflicts_with_place: full borrow, CONFLICT\\\");\\n283:         true\\n284:     }\\n285: }\\n286: \\n287: // Given that the bases of `elem1` and `elem2` are always either equal\\n288: // or disjoint (and have the same type!), return the overlap situation\\n289: // between `elem1` and `elem2`.\\n290: fn place_projection_conflict<'tcx>(\\n291:     tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\\n292:     body: &Body<'tcx>,\\n293:     pi1: PlaceRef<'tcx>,\\n294:     pi1_elem: PlaceElem<'tcx>,\\n295:     pi2_elem: PlaceElem<'tcx>,\\n296:     bias: PlaceConflictBias,\\n297: ) -> Overlap {\\n298:     match (pi1_elem, pi2_elem) {\\n299:         (ProjectionElem::Deref, ProjectionElem::Deref) => {\\n300:             // derefs (e.g., `*x` vs. `*x`) - recur.\\n301:             debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-OR-EQ-DEREF\\\");\\n302:             Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint\\n303:         }\\n304:         (ProjectionElem::OpaqueCast(_), ProjectionElem::OpaqueCast(_)) => {\\n305:             // casts to other types may always conflict irrespective of the type being cast to.\\n306:             debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-OR-EQ-OPAQUE\\\");\\n307:             Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint\\n308:         }\\n309:         (ProjectionElem::Field(f1, _), ProjectionElem::Field(f2, _)) => {\\n310:             if f1 == f2 {\\n311:                 // same field (e.g., `a.y` vs. `a.y`) - we *do* allow\\n334:             // this code to compile:\\n335:             //\\n336:             // ```\\n337:             // fn foo(x: &mut Result<i32, i32>) {\\n338:             //     let mut v = None;\\n339:             //     if let Ok(ref mut a) = *x {\\n340:             //         v = Some(a);\\n341:             //     }\\n342:             //     // here, you would *think* that the\\n343:             //     // *entirety* of `x` would be borrowed,\\n344:             //     // but in fact only the `Ok` variant is,\\n345:             //     // so the `Err` variant is *entirely free*:\\n346:             //     if let Err(ref mut a) = *x {\\n347:             //         v = Some(a);\\n348:             //     }\\n349:             //     drop(v);\\n350:             // }\\n351:             // ```\\n352:             if v1 == v2 {\\n353:                 debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-OR-EQ-FIELD\\\");\\n354:                 Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint\\n355:             } else {\\n356:                 debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-FIELD\\\");\\n357:                 Overlap::Disjoint\\n358:             }\\n359:         }\\n360:         (\\n361:             ProjectionElem::Index(..),\\n362:             ProjectionElem::Index(..)\\n363:             | ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { .. }\\n364:             | ProjectionElem::Subslice { .. },\\n365:         )\\n366:         | (\\n367:             ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { .. } | ProjectionElem::Subslice { .. },\\n368:             ProjectionElem::Index(..),\\n369:         ) => {\\n370:             // Array indexes (`a[0]` vs. `a[i]`). These can either be disjoint\\n371:             // (if the indexes differ) or equal (if they are the same).\\n372:             match bias {\\n373:                 PlaceConflictBias::Overlap => {\\n374:                     // If we are biased towards overlapping, then this is the recursive\\n375:                     // case that gives \\\"equal *or* disjoint\\\" its meaning.\\n376:                     debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-OR-EQ-ARRAY-INDEX\\\");\\n377:                     Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint\\n378:                 }\\n379:                 PlaceConflictBias::NoOverlap => {\\n380:                     // If we are biased towards no overlapping, then this is disjoint.\\n381:                     debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict:     "content": "1: //! The borrowck rules for proving disjointness are applied from the \"root\" of the\n2: //! borrow forwards, iterating over \"similar\" projections in lockstep until\n3: //! we can prove overlap one way or another. Essentially, we treat `Overlap` as\n4: //! a monoid and report a conflict if the product ends up not being `Disjoint`.\n5: //!\n6: //! On each step, if we didn't run out of borrow or place, we know that our elements\n7: //! have the same type, and that they only overlap if they are the identical.\n8: //!\n9: //! For example, if we are comparing these:\n10: //! ```text\n11: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\n12: //! ACCESS:  (*x1[i].y).w.b\n13: //! ```\n14: //!\n15: //! Then our steps are:\n16: //! ```text\n17: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\n18: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\n19: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\n20: //!      *x1[2].y    |  *x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\n21: //!     (*x1[2].y).z | (*x1[i].y).w  -- we are disjoint and don't need to check more!\n22: //! ```\n23: //!\n24: //! Because `zip` does potentially bad things to the iterator inside, this loop\n25: //! also handles the case where the access might be a *prefix* of the borrow, e.g.\n26: //!\n27: //! ```text\n28: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\n29: //! ACCESS:  x1[i].y\n30: //! ```\n31: //!\n32: //! Then our steps are:\n33: //! ```text\n34: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\n35: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\n36: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\n37: //! ```\n38: //!\n39: //! -- here we run out of access - the borrow can access a part of it. If this\n40: //! is a full deep access, then we *know* the borrow conflicts with it. However,\n41: //! if the access is shallow, then we can proceed:\n42: //!\n43: //! ```text\n44: //!       x1[2].y    | (*x1[i].y)    -- a deref! the access can't get past this, so we\n45: //!                                     are disjoint\n46: //! ```\n47: //!\n48: //! Our invariant is, that at each step of the iteration:\n49: //!  - If we didn't run out of access to match, our borrow and access are comparable\n50: //!    and either equal or disjoint.\n51: //!  - If we did run out of access, the borrow can access a part of it.\n52: \n53: use std::cmp::max;\n54: use std::iter;\n55: \n56: use rustc_hir as hir;\n57: use rustc_middle::bug;\n58: use rustc_middle::mir::{\n59:     Body, BorrowKind, FakeBorrowKind, MutBorrowKind, Place, PlaceElem, PlaceRef, ProjectionElem,\n60: };\n61: use rustc_middle::ty::{self, TyCtxt};\n62: use tracing::{debug, instrument};\n63: \n64: use crate::{AccessDepth, ArtificialField, Deep, Overlap, Shallow};\n65: \n66: /// When checking if a place conflicts with another place, this enum is used to influence decisions\n67: /// where a place might be equal or disjoint with another place, such as if `a[i] == a[j]`.\n68: /// `PlaceConflictBias::Overlap` would bias toward assuming that `i` might equal `j` and that these\n69: /// places overlap. `PlaceConflictBias::NoOverlap` assumes that for the purposes of the predicate\n70: /// being run in the calling context, the conservative choice is to assume the compared indices\n71: /// are disjoint (and therefore, do not overlap).\n72: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug, Eq, PartialEq)]\n73: pub enum PlaceConflictBias {\n74:     Overlap,\n75:     NoOverlap,\n76: }\n77: \n78: /// Helper function for checking if places conflict with a mutable borrow and deep access depth.\n79: /// This is used to check for places conflicting outside of the borrow checking code (such as in\n80: /// dataflow).\n81: pub fn places_conflict<'tcx>(\n82:     tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n83:     body: &Body<'tcx>,\n84:     borrow_place: Place<'tcx>,\n85:     access_place: Place<'tcx>,\n86:     bias: PlaceConflictBias,\n87: ) -> bool {\n88:     borrow_conflicts_with_place(\n89:         tcx,\n90:         body,\n91:         borrow_place,\n92:         BorrowKind::Mut { kind: MutBorrowKind::TwoPhaseBorrow },\n93:         access_place.as_ref(),\n94:         AccessDepth::Deep,\n95:         bias,\n96:     )\n97: }\n98: \n99: /// Checks whether the `borrow_place` conflicts with the `access_place` given a borrow kind and\n100: /// access depth. The `bias` parameter is used to determine how the unknowable (comparing runtime\n101: /// array indices, for example) should be interpreted - this depends on what the caller wants in\n102: /// order to make the conservative choice and preserve soundness.\n103: #[inline]\n104: pub(super) fn borrow_conflicts_with_place<'tcx>(\n105:     tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n106:     body: &Body<'tcx>,\n107:     borrow_place: Place<'tcx>,\n108:     borrow_kind: BorrowKind,\n109:     access_place: PlaceRef<'tcx>,\n110:     access: AccessDepth,\n111:     bias: PlaceConflictBias,\n112: ) -> bool {\n113:     let borrow_local = borrow_place.local;\n114:     let access_local = access_place.local;\n115: \n116:     if borrow_local != access_local {\n117:         // We have proven the borrow disjoint - further projections will remain disjoint.\n118:         return false;\n119:     }\n120: \n121:     // This Local/Local case is handled by the more general code below, but\n122:     // it's so common that it's a speed win to check for it first.\n123:     if borrow_place.projection.is_empty() && access_place.projection.is_empty() {\n124:         return true;\n125:     }\n126: \n127:     place_components_conflict(tcx, body, borrow_place, borrow_kind, access_place, access, bias)\n128: }\n129: \n130: #[instrument(level = \"debug\", skip(tcx, body))]\n131: fn place_components_conflict<'tcx>(\n132:     tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n133:     body: &Body<'tcx>,\n134:     borrow_place: Place<'tcx>,\n135:     borrow_kind: BorrowKind,\n136:     access_place: PlaceRef<'tcx>,\n137:     access: AccessDepth,\n138:     bias: PlaceConflictBias,\n139: ) -> bool {\n140:     let borrow_local = borrow_place.local;\n141:     let access_local = access_place.local;\n142:     // borrow_conflicts_with_place should have checked that.\n143:     assert_eq!(borrow_local, access_local);\n144: \n145:     // loop invariant: borrow_c is always either equal to access_c or disjoint from it.\n146:     for ((borrow_place, borrow_c), &access_c) in\n147:         iter::zip(borrow_place.iter_projections(), access_place.projection)\n148:     {\n149:         debug!(?borrow_c, ?access_c);\n150: \n151:         // Borrow and access path both have more components.\n152:         //\n153:         // Examples:\n154:         //\n155:         // - borrow of `a.(...)`, access to `a.(...)`\n156:         // - borrow of `a.(...)`, access to `b.(...)`\n157:         //\n158:         // Here we only see the components we have checked so\n159:         // far (in our examples, just the first component). We\n160:         // check whether the components being borrowed vs\n161:         // accessed are disjoint (as in the second example,\n162:         // but not the first).\n163:         match place_projection_conflict(tcx, body, borrow_place, borrow_c, access_c, bias) {\n164:             Overlap::Arbitrary => {\n165:                 // We have encountered different fields of potentially\n166:                 // the same union - the borrow now partially overlaps.\n167:                 //\n168:                 // There is no *easy* way of comparing the fields\n169:                 // further on, because they might have different types\n170:                 // (e.g., borrows of `u.a.0` and `u.b.y` where `.0` and\n171:                 // `.y` come from different structs).\n172:                 //\n173:                 // We could try to do some things here - e.g., count\n174:                 // dereferences - but that's probably not a good\n175:                 // idea, at least for now, so just give up and\n176:                 // report a conflict. This is unsafe code anyway so\n177:                 // the user could always use raw pointers.\n178:                 debug!(\"arbitrary -> conflict\");\n179:                 return true;\n180:             }\n181:             Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint => {\n182:                 // This is the recursive case - proceed to the next element.\n183:             }\n184:             Overlap::Disjoint => {\n185:                 // We have proven the borrow disjoint - further\n186:                 // projections will remain disjoint.\n187:                 debug!(\"disjoint\");\n188:                 return false;\n189:             }\n190:         }\n191:     }\n192: \n193:     if borrow_place.projection.len() > access_place.projection.len() {\n194:         for (base, elem) in borrow_place.iter_projections().skip(access_place.projection.len()) {\n195:             // Borrow path is longer than the access path. Examples:\n196:             //\n197:             // - borrow of `a.b.c`, access to `a.b`\n198:             //\n199:             // Here, we know that the borrow can access a part of\n200:             // our place. This is a conflict if that is a part our\n201:             // access cares about.\n202: \n203:             let base_ty = base.ty(body, tcx).ty;\n204: \n205:             match (elem, base_ty.kind(), access) {\n206:                 (_, _, Shallow(Some(ArtificialField::ArrayLength)))\n207:                 | (_, _, Shallow(Some(ArtificialField::FakeBorrow))) => {\n208:                     // The array length is like additional fields on the\n209:                     // type; it does not overlap any existing data there.\n210:                     // Furthermore, if cannot actually be a prefix of any\n211:                     // borrowed place (at least in MIR as it is currently.)\n212:                     //\n213:                     // e.g., a (mutable) borrow of `a[5]` while we read the\n214:                     // array length of `a`.\n215:                     debug!(\"borrow_conflicts_with_place: implicit field\");\n216:                     return false;\n217:                 }\n218: \n219:                 (ProjectionElem::Deref, _, Shallow(None)) => {\n220:                     // e.g., a borrow of `*x.y` while we shallowly access `x.y` or some\n221:                     // prefix thereof - the shallow access can't touch anything behind\n222:                     // the pointer.\n223:                     debug!(\"borrow_conflicts_with_place: shallow access behind ptr\");\n224:                     return false;\n225:                 }\n226:                 (ProjectionElem::Deref, ty::Ref(_, _, hir::Mutability::Not), _) => {\n227:                     // Shouldn't be tracked\n228:                     bug!(\"Tracking borrow behind shared reference.\");\n229:                 }\n230:                 (ProjectionElem::Deref, ty::Ref(_, _, hir::Mutability::Mut), AccessDepth::Drop) => {\n231:                     // Values behind a mutable reference are not access either by dropping a\n232:                     // value, or by StorageDead\n233:                     debug!(\"borrow_conflicts_with_place: drop access behind ptr\");\n234:                     return false;\n235:                 }\n236: \n237:                 (ProjectionElem::Field { .. }, ty::Adt(def, _), AccessDepth::Drop) => {\n238:                     // Drop can read/write arbitrary projections, so places\n239:                     // conflict regardless of further projections.\n240:                     if def.has_dtor(tcx) {\n241:                         return true;\n242:                     }\n243:                 }\n244: \n245:                 (ProjectionElem::Deref, _, Deep)\n246:                 | (ProjectionElem::Deref, _, AccessDepth::Drop)\n247:                 | (ProjectionElem::Field { .. }, _, _)\n248:                 | (ProjectionElem::Index { .. }, _, _)\n249:                 | (ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { .. }, _, _)\n250:                 | (ProjectionElem::Subslice { .. }, _, _)\n251:                 | (ProjectionElem::OpaqueCast { .. }, _, _)\n252:                 | (ProjectionElem::Downcast { .. }, _, _)\n253:                 | (ProjectionElem::UnwrapUnsafeBinder(_), _, _) => {\n254:                     // Recursive case.
